  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2b1d861b-7881-4842-9000-75e755b8664c'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer1328321692084768401"><b>The spellbinding diary of a teenage girl who escapes persecution as a witch--only to face new intolerance in a Puritan settlement.</b><br/><br/>Enter the world of young Mary Newbury, a world where simply being different can cost a person her life. Hidden until now in the pages of her diary, Mary's startling story begins in 1659, the year her beloved grandmother is hanged in the public s</span>
  <span id="freeText1328321692084768401" style="display:none"><b>The spellbinding diary of a teenage girl who escapes persecution as a witch--only to face new intolerance in a Puritan settlement.</b><br /><br />Enter the world of young Mary Newbury, a world where simply being different can cost a person her life. Hidden until now in the pages of her diary, Mary's startling story begins in 1659, the year her beloved grandmother is hanged in the public square as a witch. Mary narrowly escapes a similar fate, only to face intolerance and new danger among the Puritans in the New World. How long can she hide her true identity? Will she ever find a place where her healing powers will not be feared?<br /><br />Just two weeks after publication, Celia Rees's WITCH CHILD spirited its way onto the Book Sense Children's Only 76 list as one of the Top 10 books that independent booksellers like to handsell. Within a month, this riveting book sold out its first two hardcover printings. Now, Candlewick Press is pleased to announce the publication of WITCH CHILD in paperback.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer295315928" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10464485286198609346">The North American witch hunts of the 1600’s was a tumultuous and horrifying time in our history, particularly for women who were unable to conform to the norms of society.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380372493i/725788._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/> <br/>Witch Child is a diary of sorts that starts out with Mary, recounting the horrific and humiliating witch trial that her beloved old grandmother had to endure before her public execution in England. It follows Mary as she makes her journey to the New World where she realized that things are not much different than they were in</span>
  <span id="freeText10464485286198609346" style="display:none">The North American witch hunts of the 1600’s was a tumultuous and horrifying time in our history, particularly for women who were unable to conform to the norms of society.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380372493i/725788._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>Witch Child is a diary of sorts that starts out with Mary, recounting the horrific and humiliating witch trial that her beloved old grandmother had to endure before her public execution in England. It follows Mary as she makes her journey to the New World where she realized that things are not much different than they were in England.<br> <br><b>This is not your typical “Salem witch trial”-esque novel.</b> ( I was a bit worried it would be just another retelling of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17250.The_Crucible" title="The Crucible by Arthur Miller" rel="nofollow noopener">The Crucible</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/703292.The_Witch_Of_Blackbird_Pond" title="The Witch Of Blackbird Pond by Elizabeth George Speare" rel="nofollow noopener">The Witch Of Blackbird Pond</a> )<br>Sure it keeps in the interesting historical facts but it adds a new twist. Here is why Witch Child is original and captivating:<br>Our protagonist, Mary, is a not only a terrified puritan girl wanting to avoid being accused of witchcraft. But, <b>she is</b>, in fact, <b>a witch</b>. Well, really more like a modern-day Pagan or Wiccan. But, still, considered a full-blown witch by their standards.<br>The other thing that makes this book stand out from its contemporaries is that Rees has created a artful parallel between two cultures and thus a compelling statement about how laws, and opinions are highly influenced by society. In the woods near the city of Beulah, where Mary is living, there is a Native American people who strongly revere shamanism and second sight in their people. In stark contrast to their puritan neighbors who (as we all know) are sending many a young woman to the gallows for the same thing.<br> <br>I found this new spin on an old favorite topic compelling and engrossing despite the fact that some of the sub characters were a little flat and boring.<br> <br>If I had to choose just one word to describe Witch Child it would be <u>Enchanting</u>.<br> <br>Recommended for anyone who loves witch lore, Early American historical fiction, and/or Native American culture.<br><b>4 stars from me.</b><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="10464485286198609346" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It's not a high-paced thriller and to be honest not much actually happens, but it is a great, pleasant read, and totally compelling.<br/><br/>I love the various settings and all of the conflict which comes with them.<br/><br/>This book flirts with fantasy but there's very little outright.   <span id="freeText16509686483023997401" style="display:none"><b>5 Words: Magic, conflict, superstition, new world.</b><br /><br />This is such a great book, and I've loved it for years. It's not a high-paced thriller and to be honest not much actually happens, but it is a great, pleasant read, and totally compelling.<br /><br />I love the various settings and all of the conflict which comes with them.<br /><br />This book flirts with fantasy but there's very little outright. It not in your face, it's subtle and quite tame. It comes across as very realistic and what magic is mentioned is rather vague - it's more hedge-witchery and healing. <br /><br />I quite liked the way it was written, it was almost hesitant. It was also very clever. I like it when fiction is presented in such a way that it <i>could</i> be real.</span>

<div id="review_3505782885" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3505782885" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28602001-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438967931p2/28602001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3505782885?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/28602001-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11775436-witch-child">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28602001-emma?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3505782885" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7548297880887418402">Mary and her grandmother exist on the fringes of society, eking out a living by midwifery and herb lore. But those on the margins are always at risk from their neighbours, existing at the mercy of their good opinion. On a day like any other, Mary's grandmother is accused of witchcraft, then quickly hanged for doing nothing more than what neighbours once called 'help' but now considered to be 'crimes'. Left alone, Mary is forced to take a dangerous path, one that stretches all the way to the New </span>
  <span id="freeText7548297880887418402" style="display:none">Mary and her grandmother exist on the fringes of society, eking out a living by midwifery and herb lore. But those on the margins are always at risk from their neighbours, existing at the mercy of their good opinion. On a day like any other, Mary's grandmother is accused of witchcraft, then quickly hanged for doing nothing more than what neighbours once called 'help' but now considered to be 'crimes'. Left alone, Mary is forced to take a dangerous path, one that stretches all the way to the New World. But will she be any safer there? Her grandmother's needless death was Mary's first lesson about the power of prejudice and public opinion. There are many more to come. <br /><br />Told through Mary's 'lost' diary entires, the book follows her from Cromwellian England to Puritan America. Each moment holds the terrifying possibility that her secret may be revealed: Mary, too, is a witch. Her negotiation between her growing understanding of herself as a girl and a witch and the intolerance, suspicion, petty jealousies, and bitter rivalries of her new community is what lies at the heart of the novel. The narrative is pretty straightforward, with no real surprises, and it's only Celia Rees' creation of a strong and appealing character in Mary that gives the story its impact. While it addresses relatively dark themes, it's lightly done, a thought provoking read rather than a disturbing one.<br /><br />There's something to it though, a feeling of magic just awakened, and there's real potential for the sequel to add the depth that this was lacking. I'll certainly be reading it, I'd like to see what this young witch does next...<br /><br />ARC via Netgalley</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_45249633" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45249633" />
    <a title="Wade WDM" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/844658-wade-wdm"><img alt="Wade WDM" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561989835p2/844658.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/45249633?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wade WDM" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wade WDM" href="/user/show/844658-wade-wdm">Wade WDM</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Tina, Sarah</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer45249633&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45249633" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14769655036752994666"><i>1659. A time of fear and persecution. Mary, granddaughter of a witch, keeps a diary. It begins: I am Mary. I am a witch…<br/><br/>She sees her grandmother hanged, is rescued by a stranger, takes ship for America and finds a place in a Puritan community there. All that befalls her, she records in her diary and as she writes, she stitches the pages inside a quilt for discovery would mean death.</i><br/><br/>For a young adult book this was very good. No patronizing "teenage girl" voice that you would find in "Twilight". I</span>
  <span id="freeText14769655036752994666" style="display:none"><i>1659. A time of fear and persecution. Mary, granddaughter of a witch, keeps a diary. It begins: I am Mary. I am a witch…<br /><br />She sees her grandmother hanged, is rescued by a stranger, takes ship for America and finds a place in a Puritan community there. All that befalls her, she records in her diary and as she writes, she stitches the pages inside a quilt for discovery would mean death.</i><br /><br />For a young adult book this was very good. No patronizing "teenage girl" voice that you would find in "Twilight". I actually suggest getting a copy of the book on cd so you can hear the wonderful Jennifer Ehle (who played Elizabeth Bennett in the A&amp;E version of Pride and Prejudice) reading the story. <br /><br />It is a light read. It is a little stereotypical, but then again, doesn't history pretty much point out that the Puritans were a bit stodgy and afraid of just about anything that couldn't be explained by the local pastor? <br /><br />There were times when I felt as if the story was being outright stolen from other "witch hunt/witch trial" stories out there - some teenage girls don't like another teenage girl and they all start acting crazy and blaming the other girl for it. "She comes to me with the Devil!" That part was a little disappointing. I've read that story already. I knew sooner or later that Mary would be considered a witch and probably hunted down by her townsfolk, but to have it almost exactly like many other stories? meh...<br /><br />In the end, I thought the book on cd was entertaining, especially as I worked on boring data entry. Nothing too heavy but not too light either. Didn't draw my attention away too much from my work, but kept me interested and going. <br /><br />A definite read!<br /><br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_732344250" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/732344250" />
    <a title="Kate Forsyth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3237560-kate-forsyth"><img alt="Kate Forsyth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329268435p2/3237560.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/732344250?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate Forsyth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate Forsyth" href="/user/show/3237560-kate-forsyth">Kate Forsyth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3237560-kate-forsyth?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3237560-kate-forsyth?shelf=ya-historical">ya-historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer732344250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7306411136929731388">This wonderful historical novel for teenagers begins: ‘I am Mary. I am a witch.’ It is set in 1659, during the tumultuous months after Cromwell’s death and before the return of Charles II. Her story is purportedly told in diary entries that have been found sewn inside a quilt. It is a tragic and powerful tale, which begins when Mary’s grandmother is arrested and tortured by witch-finders and then hanged in the town square. Mary is rescued by a rich woman who she suspects may be her real mother, </span>
  <span id="freeText7306411136929731388" style="display:none">This wonderful historical novel for teenagers begins: ‘I am Mary. I am a witch.’ It is set in 1659, during the tumultuous months after Cromwell’s death and before the return of Charles II. Her story is purportedly told in diary entries that have been found sewn inside a quilt. It is a tragic and powerful tale, which begins when Mary’s grandmother is arrested and tortured by witch-finders and then hanged in the town square. Mary is rescued by a rich woman who she suspects may be her real mother, and sent to join a group of Puritans fleeing to the New World. However, the Puritans are stern and narrow-minded and quick to blame any misfortune on witchcraft. Mary finds herself in increasing danger as the party lands in Salem, Massachusetts. A growing friendship with a Native American and his shaman grandfather increases her risk. A simple yet powerful tale that explores the nature of magic and superstition, faith and cruelty.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7306411136929731388" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2016">z-read2016</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1709519917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer997129387418158544">2.5 stars. A lot of potential and good writing style, but ultimately just another boring, archetypal historical fiction. <br/><br/>When I was in my preteen stage, I went through a historical fiction stage, and I read countless books about witch hunts. Almost all of them share some major traits: a main character who is a misfit, usually because she's particularly unreligious, and a boring beginning. <br/><br/><b>Unfortunately, this book doesn't break that mold.</b> Rees breaks no boundaries with her sometimes-boring plotti</span>
  <span id="freeText997129387418158544" style="display:none">2.5 stars. A lot of potential and good writing style, but ultimately just another boring, archetypal historical fiction. <br /><br />When I was in my preteen stage, I went through a historical fiction stage, and I read countless books about witch hunts. Almost all of them share some major traits: a main character who is a misfit, usually because she's particularly unreligious, and a boring beginning. <br /><br /><b>Unfortunately, this book doesn't break that mold.</b> Rees breaks no boundaries with her sometimes-boring plotting. <br /><br />Besides the unoriginality, this book fails due to bad plotting. <b><i>Witch Child</i> is far too drawn out.</b> The first half was completely boring, and the author only manages to develop dramatic tension towards the end. <br /><br />This book does do some good things. Celia Rees' prose flows very nicely, making even the boring bits easy to read. And the main protagonist here was genuinely likable, which is definitely a redeeming factor. But altogether, there was nothing special about this book. It was just okay.</span>
  <a data-text-id="997129387418158544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_52382340" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/52382340" />
    <a title="Lily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/408298-lily"><img alt="Lily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1190560474p2/408298.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/52382340?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lily" href="/user/show/408298-lily">Lily</a>
      </span>

          added it



          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone who likes magical controversy</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer52382340" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15995640949392455923">Witch Child, by Celia Rees explores a very contradictory issue that existed in America for a vast amount of time. The Salem Witch trials are studied in classes to this day, and the events that took place still haunt many people. This novel does not focus directly or bluntly state the events of the Salem Witch Trials, but is obviously focused in that central time period. The setting of this novel is essential in the plot, which is something I do not regularly see in other texts. This unique focus</span>
  <span id="freeText15995640949392455923" style="display:none">Witch Child, by Celia Rees explores a very contradictory issue that existed in America for a vast amount of time. The Salem Witch trials are studied in classes to this day, and the events that took place still haunt many people. This novel does not focus directly or bluntly state the events of the Salem Witch Trials, but is obviously focused in that central time period. The setting of this novel is essential in the plot, which is something I do not regularly see in other texts. This unique focus on that specific literary element really intrigued me; I don't think this book would be the same if alternate literary devices had been demonstrated to portray the overall theme of hardships of witch craft.<br />Additionally, the point of view of this novel played an essential role in portraying the message Rees intended. If the narrator of this novel hadn't been a witch suffering from the mistreatment and horrors surrounding her, the readers would not be subject to bias and might hold a different opinion on the events. <br />Overall, this novel is very well written, and despite a few disturbing images that prevented me from reading it in the past, I really enjoyed this book and recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15995640949392455923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4645678775684796086">I don't think I was really in the mood for this. It's a fairly straightforward historical fiction, with a fairly standard frame story of a found diary type deal. It's very easy to read; definitely aimed at young adults, if not at kids. Probably that's part of it -- it was so easy there was nothing to hold onto. The set-up is interesting enough, and for what it is, it's well-written, but there wasn't enough substance for me.</span>

<div id="review_161910950" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/161910950" />
    <a title="TheBookAddictedGirl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5009509-thebookaddictedgirl"><img alt="TheBookAddictedGirl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1429733485p2/5009509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/161910950?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TheBookAddictedGirl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TheBookAddictedGirl" href="/user/show/5009509-thebookaddictedgirl">TheBookAddictedGirl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408800263" href="/book/show/7329683-witch-child">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone Over 11 Who Love Powerful Characters, Magic, And Historical Fiction You Can't Put Down!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5009509-thebookaddictedgirl?shelf=british-fiction">british-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5009509-thebookaddictedgirl?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5009509-thebookaddictedgirl?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5009509-thebookaddictedgirl?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5009509-thebookaddictedgirl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5009509-thebookaddictedgirl?shelf=pre-teen">pre-teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5009509-thebookaddictedgirl?shelf=ya-child-crossover">ya-child-crossover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5009509-thebookaddictedgirl?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5009509-thebookaddictedgirl?shelf=magic">magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer161910950" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17338444456445125580">“I am Mary. I am a witch.”<br/><br/>Witch Child tells the story of a girl named Mary, whose grandmother was hanged for being a witch. She had to leave, before the townspeople turned on her as well. And so she was taken away from the only home she’s know by a mysterious woman she’s never met, Mary is sent to America for her own safety. But life aboard a ship of Puritans heading to the New World is just as dangerous as it was back home in England – maybe more so. Can she keep her secret? Or will she be disc</span>
  <span id="freeText17338444456445125580" style="display:none">“I am Mary. I am a witch.”<br /><br />Witch Child tells the story of a girl named Mary, whose grandmother was hanged for being a witch. She had to leave, before the townspeople turned on her as well. And so she was taken away from the only home she’s know by a mysterious woman she’s never met, Mary is sent to America for her own safety. But life aboard a ship of Puritans heading to the New World is just as dangerous as it was back home in England – maybe more so. Can she keep her secret? Or will she be discovered, and killed just as her grandmother was?<br /><br />I was captivated, and literally devoured Witch Child. It was an amazing, powerful story, and was also insanely addictive. <br /><br />Told from Mary’s point of view, it’s written in the form of a diary that was found sewn into the seams of a quilt. As I read, I felt like I had travelled back to the 1600s, and there were loads of little details that just made the history feel alive. <br /><br />Mary was a brilliant character, strong and brave. I loved her spirit, and found myself feeling everything she felt. Her voice was unique, and her emotions intense: she was an entirely believable character.<br /><br />The supporting characters were brilliant as well, and all very real. Jaybird, the Native American Indian boy; Martha, the Puritan who took Mary in; Reverend Johnson, the one who believes he’s a prophet of God, who I believe is really the evil one. There were so many amazing characters, and they all went together to form a brilliant, realistic world.<br /><br />The thing I liked most about this book was the history behind it. The witch trials both fascinate and horrify me, ever since I learnt about them at the very beginning of high school. It amazes me how narrow minded people can be, and how healers can be seen as “spawn of the Devil”. Did you know that at least 250,000 women were killed, and in some villages were left with no women at all? (I’d just like to point out that I didn’t actually get that from the book, it’s just a weird piece of information that I’ve remembered, for some reason or another.) And the Native American Indian history and beliefs intrigued me too: how the settlers forced them out, their ideas on spirits, the way they live. I wouldn’t have thought that the two would go together so well, but they did, and I loved the way they did.<br /><br />The one and only downside: the concept of magic and witchcraft was left unclear. Mary hinted at visions, controlling storms and voodoo-like dolls, but nothing was confirmed... Unless that’s what Celia Rees meant for it to be like... to make you think, to wonder...<br /><br />Overall, Witch Child was a brilliantly written story with authentic, unique characters and an amazing plot. It was intense, addictive and ended with a horrible cliffhanger. Even though it’s written for 11+, I think everyone can enjoy the history in it!<br /><br />Finally, a simple question:<br />Do you believe in magic?</span>
  <a data-text-id="17338444456445125580" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2813479348" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2813479348" />
    <a title="Celia Buell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29892659-celia-buell"><img alt="Celia Buell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550789566p2/29892659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2813479348?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celia Buell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celia Buell" href="/user/show/29892659-celia-buell">Celia Buell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29892659-celia-buell?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29892659-celia-buell?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29892659-celia-buell?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29892659-celia-buell?shelf=adoption">adoption</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29892659-celia-buell?shelf=to-reread">to-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29892659-celia-buell?shelf=america">america</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29892659-celia-buell?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29892659-celia-buell?shelf=first-in-a-series">first-in-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29892659-celia-buell?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29892659-celia-buell?shelf=strong-women">strong-women</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2813479348" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18159102730112688020">I don't know a lot about the 1600s and the various "witch trials" and fear that ran throughout England and the colonies, and what I do know comes from Shakespeare and from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17250.The_Crucible' title='The Crucible by Arthur Miller' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Crucible</a>, both which show all the accusation with no truth to any of it.<br/><br/>But <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/83085.Celia_Rees' title='Celia Rees' rel='nofollow noopener'>Celia Rees</a> turns the known story on its head, where suddenly, witches are real, and they know who they are. The main character, Mary, who has true powers, has escaped persecution in Britain on a Puritan ship headed to the New World, but what she do</span>
  <span id="freeText18159102730112688020" style="display:none">I don't know a lot about the 1600s and the various "witch trials" and fear that ran throughout England and the colonies, and what I do know comes from Shakespeare and from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17250.The_Crucible" title="The Crucible by Arthur Miller" rel="nofollow noopener">The Crucible</a>, both which show all the accusation with no truth to any of it.<br /><br />But <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/83085.Celia_Rees" title="Celia Rees" rel="nofollow noopener">Celia Rees</a> turns the known story on its head, where suddenly, witches are real, and they know who they are. The main character, Mary, who has true powers, has escaped persecution in Britain on a Puritan ship headed to the New World, but what she doesn't know is that she will face even worse there.<br /><br />I loved the character development and the ways that Mary's friends become her family. At first it doesn't seem like there's much in the way of character development, and the voice is kind of hard to read, but by the end you realize that each significant character has actually changed a lot, and people start to question their own values and their devotion to a community that will treat one of their own in this way.<br /><br />I feel like I learned a lot more about the general contrast between indigenous beliefs and Christianity, and the ways they clashed originally. Living in a modern and very diverse community, and being a nonreligious and spiritually questioning person, I have always found this clash and the fear of Native Americans as witches hard to believe, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/803120.Witch_Child__Witch_Child___1_" title="Witch Child (Witch Child, #1) by Celia Rees" rel="nofollow noopener">Witch Child</a> clears some of that up in ways that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17250.The_Crucible" title="The Crucible by Arthur Miller" rel="nofollow noopener">The Crucible</a> didn't. I understand the fear-mongering and the need to blame someone better after reading this book, and getting the perspective of a girl who actually has the powers she is accused of having.<br /><br />The story leaves off, literally, in the middle of a sentence. I had forgotten that there was going to be a sequel, but the way <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/803120.Witch_Child__Witch_Child___1_" title="Witch Child (Witch Child, #1) by Celia Rees" rel="nofollow noopener">Witch Child</a> ended makes me so anxious to get my hands on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/300017.Sorceress__Witch_Child___2_" title="Sorceress (Witch Child, #2) by Celia Rees" rel="nofollow noopener">Sorceress</a> as soon as I can. I know I start so many series that I don't end up continuing for months or years, but I want this to be different. I wish I actually owned the book, but I'll find a way. I will definitely try to read it this summer.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18159102730112688020" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_76821566" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/76821566" />
    <a title="NSAndrew Liebergen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2750253-nsandrew-liebergen"><img alt="NSAndrew Liebergen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1253824250p2/2750253.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/76821566?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="NSAndrew Liebergen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="NSAndrew Liebergen" href="/user/show/2750253-nsandrew-liebergen">NSAndrew Liebergen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2750253-nsandrew-liebergen?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer76821566" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2791746341985359648">This was my favorite book to read this week. I don’t know why, it just was the story that engrossed me into the book. You all should read this book. It is kind of a cross between a documentary, thriller, and a love story. I believe our current students would extremely enjoy this book. With the popularity of vampires and Harry Potter, children will love the supernatural aspect of this book. Teachers will love the historical facts and situations interwoven into the story. <br/>The main character Mary N</span>
  <span id="freeText2791746341985359648" style="display:none">This was my favorite book to read this week. I don’t know why, it just was the story that engrossed me into the book. You all should read this book. It is kind of a cross between a documentary, thriller, and a love story. I believe our current students would extremely enjoy this book. With the popularity of vampires and Harry Potter, children will love the supernatural aspect of this book. Teachers will love the historical facts and situations interwoven into the story. <br />The main character Mary Newbury, discovers she has supernatural powers. The text is written so eloquently, that it flows like hot butter. Mary has a grandmother who is hanged for being a witch. Mary is shipped off to the New World for safety reasons. Once there, she begins to keep a journal of her 18-month adventure in Salem, Massachusetts. <br />This is definitely a coming of age story. Celia Rees the author leads the reader through the trials and tribulations of Mary’s life. The reader sees how she deals with each situation, revealing details about Mary’s true nature. Mary’s gift is what she calls “The Sight”. Through Rees’s writing, demonstrates the many variations of the word sight. Mary seems to be able to see into a person’s emotions. <br />I also liked the fact that the book is a diary, but worked as a novel. The story is full of good research (as far as I can tell) of the time period of seventeenth century America. I liked the fact that dates and events coincided and made sense with the historical facts.<br />Witch child is a great way to intertwine fiction and history. Smooth reading and an interesting plot will make this a great read for any child in middle school.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2791746341985359648" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_570378882" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/570378882" />
    <a title="Charlotte Jones" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8943949-charlotte-jones"><img alt="Charlotte Jones" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361900141p2/8943949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/570378882?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte Jones" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte Jones" href="/user/show/8943949-charlotte-jones">Charlotte Jones</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780747550099" href="/book/show/1099080.Witch_Child">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer570378882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11844269566261559639">Despite the very mixed reviews on Goodreads, I found this book gripping, entertaining anda real page turner. Firstly, I was immediately drawn in by the cover. Usually I prefer books with illustrated covers, but I found that the photograph on this and the sepia tones really reflect the feel and atmostphere of the book. <br/><br/>With regards to the premise and the style of writing, this book contains diary entries written by Mary, the granddaughter of a witch, around 1659-1660. It is regarded as a children</span>
  <span id="freeText11844269566261559639" style="display:none">Despite the very mixed reviews on Goodreads, I found this book gripping, entertaining anda real page turner. Firstly, I was immediately drawn in by the cover. Usually I prefer books with illustrated covers, but I found that the photograph on this and the sepia tones really reflect the feel and atmostphere of the book. <br /><br />With regards to the premise and the style of writing, this book contains diary entries written by Mary, the granddaughter of a witch, around 1659-1660. It is regarded as a children's book, being shortlisted for the Guardian Children's Fiction prize in 2001, but I think it would definitely be suitable for a teenage or even adult audience also. As this book is not a work of fiction, more passages from an irregularly kept diary dating back from the colonial period, more commonly known as 'the Mary papers', I found some of the chapters very emotional and thought-provoking, as I knew they were based on reality. <br /><br />I am finding it difficult to write a review for this book, as I honestly cannot fault it in any way. I loved the simplistic yet poetic writing style, the story that this girl lived and also the characters that she met along the way. 'Witch Child' by Celia Rees is a definite 5 out of 5 stars for me, and I would thoroughly recommend it to readers of any age, as I think it gives an important lesson in the superstitions and cruelties of human nature, and is a beautiful quick read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11844269566261559639" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_460695068" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/460695068" />
    <a title="Beth Bonini" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3106785-beth-bonini"><img alt="Beth Bonini" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444482564p2/3106785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/460695068?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth Bonini" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth Bonini" href="/user/show/3106785-beth-bonini">Beth Bonini</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3106785-beth-bonini?shelf=children-s-book-club">children-s-book-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer460695068" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6205488367219494918">This is a particularly compelling example of historical fiction. So compelling, in fact,that I think my students may well ask, "Is this real?" I have to continually explain that good fiction SHOULD convince you that "it" (the characters, the emotions, the storyline) is "real," but sometimes they find that concept confusing. Well, author Celia Rees does a terrific job of making you feel like a historian/anthropologist who has just discovered an amazing find: the diary of a young colonial girl whi</span>
  <span id="freeText6205488367219494918" style="display:none">This is a particularly compelling example of historical fiction. So compelling, in fact,that I think my students may well ask, "Is this real?" I have to continually explain that good fiction SHOULD convince you that "it" (the characters, the emotions, the storyline) is "real," but sometimes they find that concept confusing. Well, author Celia Rees does a terrific job of making you feel like a historian/anthropologist who has just discovered an amazing find: the diary of a young colonial girl which has been stitched into a quilt. Mary Newbury's story begins in Cromwellian England, and the action begins in the first chapter when Mary's grandmother is hanged for practising witchcraft. Mary is whisked away by a mysterious woman, and then given into the care of some Puritans who are sailing for the New World. Mary's grandmother has been a herbalist and healer, and Mary has learned -- and has need to practise -- some of these healing skills. Before long, though, whispers that she is a witch begin to undermine her tentative place in this new community. <br /><br />Full of wonderful details, beautifully written, and possessing an interesting, consistent narrative voice, this is a story that should appeal to most female readers. Although Rees writes for young adults, this book has the sophistication to appeal to adult readers as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6205488367219494918" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2112170383" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2112170383" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2112170383?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Bursting Bookshelf of a Wallflower" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Bursting Bookshelf of a Wallflower" href="/user/show/29402776-the-bursting-bookshelf-of-a-wallflower">The Bursting Bookshelf of a Wallflower</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Taschenbuch 9783401028545" href="/book/show/1634854.Hexenkind">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2112170383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6091406309142569305"><b>3.5 stars!</b> <br/><br/>When her grandmother is accused for sorcery, <b>Mary</b> has to flee immediately. With the help of a mysterious woman, she is able to get on a boat that is leaving the continent for the <b>New World</b>. Living within <b>a puritan settlement</b>, Mary is however once again the target of hatred and persecution. Will her friends be able to protect her? <br/><br/>I have always been intersted in reading about the persecution of whiches and sorceres as one of the darkest chapters in human history and I remember that I e</span>
  <span id="freeText6091406309142569305" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars!</b> <br /><br />When her grandmother is accused for sorcery, <b>Mary</b> has to flee immediately. With the help of a mysterious woman, she is able to get on a boat that is leaving the continent for the <b>New World</b>. Living within <b>a puritan settlement</b>, Mary is however once again the target of hatred and persecution. Will her friends be able to protect her? <br /><br />I have always been intersted in reading about the persecution of whiches and sorceres as one of the darkest chapters in human history and I remember that I enjoyed reading this book a lot as a teenager. <b>Mary is an intriguing character</b> and I desperately wanted to know all about her. Unfortunately, the story is focusing a lot on her travel over sea and on the settlement of the group of puritans. When the story is suddenly getting suspenseful, I had the feeling that the author rushed a little through it and the ending came much too fast! <br /><br />Considering that the story is having an <b>open end</b>, the many important happening in the last few pages left me a little unsatisfied. After having read the reviews of the second installment of this series - which is supposed to wrap up the fate of Mary - I am however unsure if I am going to give the book a try. I guess that the little hints I got by reading the blurb and the reviews gave me all the information I wanted to have.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6091406309142569305" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_195117746" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/195117746" />
    <a title="Relyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1060439-relyn"><img alt="Relyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562432472p2/1060439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/195117746?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Relyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Relyn" href="/user/show/1060439-relyn">Relyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">teen lit lovers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Relyn by: </span>
      spotted at a Phoenix used book shop
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer195117746" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer217346354750548875">One of the things I was really looking forward to about this vacation is all the time in the car to read. Humph! I didn't bring a single book that I wanted to read. No kidding. At the time I packed, I was tired and I grabbed really light reading. When it came time to read, I really wanted a <i>story</i>, you know? Instead, I read all my magazines and bought more. <br/><br/>One of the things Jeffrey and I always do in a new city is go to the art museum and seek out good used bookstores. I found this one at Bards </span>
  <span id="freeText217346354750548875" style="display:none">One of the things I was really looking forward to about this vacation is all the time in the car to read. Humph! I didn't bring a single book that I wanted to read. No kidding. At the time I packed, I was tired and I grabbed really light reading. When it came time to read, I really wanted a <i>story</i>, you know? Instead, I read all my magazines and bought more. <br /><br />One of the things Jeffrey and I always do in a new city is go to the art museum and seek out good used bookstores. I found this one at Bards Books in Phoenix. It is kind of fun because it's a copy actually printed in Britain and the price is listed in pounds. I read this all the way through yesterday - couldn't put it down. SO GOOD!! <br /><br />The story is another version of <i>The Crucible</i> and the Salem Witch Trials. But, somehow, it's not the same - it's compelling and a nail-biter and different. I loved this book. For one thing, she really is a witch. No worries - I didn't spoil anything. The first line of the book is something like, "I am Mary. I am a witch." There are other twists that I enjoyed, but you'll have to discover them for yourself. Great read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="217346354750548875" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2675555281" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Jessaca Willis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6635921-jessaca-willis"><img alt="Jessaca Willis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589330608p2/6635921.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2675555281?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessaca Willis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessaca Willis" href="/user/show/6635921-jessaca-willis">Jessaca Willis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6635921-jessaca-willis?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6635921-jessaca-willis?shelf=historical-fantasy-17th-centuray">historical-fantasy-17th-centuray</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2675555281" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17699680393213056041">It’s strange to read a book about witches, where the main character is a witch, and to only ever see magic twice (one of those times being 90% through the book). <br/><br/><b><i>Witch Child</i> is solidly in the historical genre, and only mildly in paranormal</b>, so if you’re looking for a story about witches, this ain’t it.<br/><br/>The only reason someone would ever want to read the journal of a witch is if there was mention of witchcraft or some cool sorceries. Mary’s journal though, is mostly about her migration to America </span>
  <span id="freeText17699680393213056041" style="display:none">It’s strange to read a book about witches, where the main character is a witch, and to only ever see magic twice (one of those times being 90% through the book). <br /><br /><b><i>Witch Child</i> is solidly in the historical genre, and only mildly in paranormal</b>, so if you’re looking for a story about witches, this ain’t it.<br /><br />The only reason someone would ever want to read the journal of a witch is if there was mention of witchcraft or some cool sorceries. Mary’s journal though, is mostly about her migration to America and settling in a Puritan settlement. <b>I might’ve actually liked the book more if it was classified as historical fiction instead of historical paranormal.</b><br /><br />I was kind of angry about this book though. You don’t get to use the format of a journal, but then include conversations and dialogue as if it were in the present. Were she writing a diary, she’d write them in past tense, at the very least. <b>I found the structure of the novel confusing and unrealistic.</b><br /><br />At least the writing itself wasn’t terrible... I did enjoy the tone of <i>Witch Child</i> and felt <b>the speech patterns were authentic to the time</b>. It’s probably the only thing that saved this book from a two star rating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17699680393213056041" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2854734657" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2854734657" />
    <a title="Pages For Thoughts" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44569789-pages-for-thoughts"><img alt="Pages For Thoughts" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580682737p2/44569789.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2854734657?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pages For Thoughts" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pages For Thoughts" href="/user/show/44569789-pages-for-thoughts">Pages For Thoughts</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44569789-pages-for-thoughts?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44569789-pages-for-thoughts?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44569789-pages-for-thoughts?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2854734657" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17452740638435008065">The format to make Witch Child a diary was very clever. As the writing felt so true and innocent, I was shocked to find out after googling that Mary Newbury actually did not exist. The air of mystery surrounding her was magnificent, and I love the uncertainty behind whether or not she is actually a witch. Some of the instances in which she has "powers" seem to be hasty judgements on the part of the townspeople- but then towards the end of the book I started to really believe that she does truly </span>
  <span id="freeText17452740638435008065" style="display:none">The format to make Witch Child a diary was very clever. As the writing felt so true and innocent, I was shocked to find out after googling that Mary Newbury actually did not exist. The air of mystery surrounding her was magnificent, and I love the uncertainty behind whether or not she is actually a witch. Some of the instances in which she has "powers" seem to be hasty judgements on the part of the townspeople- but then towards the end of the book I started to really believe that she does truly have magical powers. <br /><br />Something else I loved was the whole topic of the Witch Trials themselves. I enjoyed how clearly this book showcased some of the cruel attitudes of society and their stereotypes regarding outsiders. Those days were no stranger to prejudice and discrimination, and I loved those themes. There were certainly some creepy scenes near the end, and I loved the paranormal climax! The author has major talent in building suspense.<br /><br />However, I did have some issues with Witch Child. In many instances the plot felt weak and at an almost boring standstill. Many themes were slightly underdeveloped. It was also difficult understand at times, and near the end, almost too bizarre. While I did enjoy the mystery of whether or not Mary is written to have powers, it made the text slightly confusing as the author's note at the end and introduction made it seem nonfiction. I think Rees could have made what genre Witch Child is more clearly.<br /><br />You can see this review and more at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://pagesforthoughts.blogspot.com/2020/03/witch-child-witch-child-1-by-celia-rees.html">https://pagesforthoughts.blogspot.com...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17452740638435008065" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2002558008" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2002558008" />
    <a title="Jack Stark" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10247419-jack-stark"><img alt="Jack Stark" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590503522p2/10247419.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2002558008?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jack Stark" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jack Stark" href="/user/show/10247419-jack-stark">Jack Stark</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11775436-witch-child">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10247419-jack-stark?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10247419-jack-stark?shelf=witches">witches</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2002558008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16816713238816836082">3.6279 stars<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>They did not want her drowning, because that would deprive the people of a hanging.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Witch Child is presented as a collection of found journal entries written by Mary Newbury between March 1659 and October 1660. Mary comes from a family of witches and therefore defines herself as a witch (even though she doesn’t really practice much). After Mary’s grandmother is hanged she must flee to avoid the same fate. She boards a ship to the New World where she hopes to leave behind her witch</span>
  <span id="freeText16816713238816836082" style="display:none">3.6279 stars<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>They did not want her drowning, because that would deprive the people of a hanging.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Witch Child is presented as a collection of found journal entries written by Mary Newbury between March 1659 and October 1660. Mary comes from a family of witches and therefore defines herself as a witch (even though she doesn’t really practice much). After Mary’s grandmother is hanged she must flee to avoid the same fate. She boards a ship to the New World where she hopes to leave behind her witchy ways and live a life of freedom and free of persecution. Unfortunately, this is Puritan America… <i>need I say more?!</i><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>We are truly in the wilderness. Screeching and howlings rend the night. The cries are of creatures unknown to us, not heard in England since ages past.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I love stories of historical witches, and I have an interest in 17C America, so I was like a pig in muck with this. <i>(Picture that. Picture me, dressed in a pig suit, rolling in mud. You’re welcome.)</i> I really enjoyed going on the journey with Mary. I also enjoyed the tough, no nonsense Martha. There are aspects of magical realism which ticks another huge yes please box for me. <b>Give me more magical realism please! Om nom nom.</b> <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>I have seen his past. I have seen his future. I know how death will come to him and I feel the knowledge like a burden. Grandmother said never to reveal the manner of someone’s dying. There is no help and no avoidance. What will be, will be, but to know too soon will colour someone’s life, darkening the hue for them, stealing the light.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />There really isn’t too much that happens in this. It’s really a coming of age story. It’s a slow burner and if the setting doesn’t interest you, I think it would be easy to get bored with it. There also isn’t much mystery, action, or tension. Because we are all really smart, we all know when we read a story about historical witches what is going to happen and unfortunately, <b>this doesn’t break the mould.</b> <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>To be a midwife, to be a healer, brings danger. If everything goes well, then all are grateful, but when things go wrong, as they do often enough, well, that is a different matter. Those that heal can harm, that’s what they whisper, those that cure can kill.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />There isn’t much more to say about this. It isn’t breaking any new ground and probably won’t leave a lasting impression on me. But, I enjoyed it nonetheless. I may read the sequel as I am interested to know what happens next.<br /><br /><b>Check out this review on my blog</b> - <a href="randommelonreads.com/2017/10/29/wc-cr/" rel="nofollow noopener">Random Melon Reads</a> | Be my friend and chat with me on the <a href="https://twitter.com/ItsCJstark" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter dot com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16816713238816836082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1835182311" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1835182311" />
    <a title="Fred" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62404723-fred"><img alt="Fred" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481967776p2/62404723.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1835182311?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fred" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fred" href="/user/show/62404723-fred">Fred</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62404723-fred?shelf=assigned-reading">assigned-reading</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1835182311&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1835182311" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer742005080328467562">I wrote this review months ago! It was a book I read a long time ago and absolutely hated. I initially gave it two stars but I saw no point in it whatsoever so I come back to it all these months later and give it one star. (Not a rating I use often)<br/><br/>ORIGINAL REVIEW (far too temperate - I was just starting out!):<br/>With my acting troupe, there were a couple of terms last year when we were doing a play called The Crucible, around two terms worth of work on The Crucible. Both Witch Child and The Crucib</span>
  <span id="freeText742005080328467562" style="display:none">I wrote this review months ago! It was a book I read a long time ago and absolutely hated. I initially gave it two stars but I saw no point in it whatsoever so I come back to it all these months later and give it one star. (Not a rating I use often)<br /><br />ORIGINAL REVIEW (far too temperate - I was just starting out!):<br />With my acting troupe, there were a couple of terms last year when we were doing a play called The Crucible, around two terms worth of work on The Crucible. Both Witch Child and The Crucible deal with quite similar topics: people being accused of being witches and injustice and dishonesty etc. But the thing is with The Crucible was that I did work on it knowing that it was its own story in its own right which most stories are but I really don’t like books that are just copying other books so blatantly. And Witch Child just read like such a discount Crucible: the plotline is so similar and so copied, particularly in one of the final few scenes in Witch Child. There is a court scene where Mary, a teenage girl, is being accused of being a witch and she is found guilty and this scene in the book is practically identical to the scene in The Crucible where there is a court case and a woman called Mary (coincidence?) was being accused of being a witch in the exact same fashion. It’s identical in dialogue and identical in description: in both, there is a group of girls who are pretending to be overcome by witchcraft in order to make out that this girl is possessing them and in both scenes, they say exactly the same things, literally! In addition, I didn’t like the writing style of this book: everything was just implied too much and everything was just dealt with so subtly that at many points in the book, I struggled to wonder if anything was actually going on, I was just lost. <br /><br /> I was not enjoying this book at first so I would drag myself through this and just wait for that page number to come up meaning that I could stop. But then, I was reading exhaustedly and suddenly the book got to a point when suddenly interesting things started happening: relevant, exciting, dramatic, climactic things started happening in the story that hooked me and made me want to read further. This made the book so much more interesting than it was before and it changed my opinion of this book dramatically. So to anyone who is considering reading this book, don’t go into it with really high expectations because it’s not a great book but at least plot-wise it does get better towards the end. So that’s why it got the two stars but to be honest I didn’t like it that much.</span>
  <a data-text-id="742005080328467562" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_855407856" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/855407856" />
    <a title="Susan Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8245824-susan-rose"><img alt="Susan Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483966357p2/8245824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/855407856?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan Rose" href="/user/show/8245824-susan-rose">Susan Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer855407856" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4667734411976276914"><b>Plot:</b> This is the story of Mary a British teenager living in the time of the restoration of the monarchy.After he grandmother is accuse of witchcraft who is sent to live in the American colony of Salem. <br/><br/><b>Favourite Quote:</b> <i>'If I had any power, any at all, I would destroy them all, right here and now. I would turn them into mass of fornicating toads. I would turn them into leprous blind newts and set them to eat themselves. I would cover their bodies with suppurating plague sores. I would curse them</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4667734411976276914" style="display:none"><b>Plot:</b> This is the story of Mary a British teenager living in the time of the restoration of the monarchy.After he grandmother is accuse of witchcraft who is sent to live in the American colony of Salem. <br /><br /><b>Favourite Quote:</b> <i>'If I had any power, any at all, I would destroy them all, right here and now. I would turn them into mass of fornicating toads. I would turn them into leprous blind newts and set them to eat themselves. I would cover their bodies with suppurating plague sores. I would curse them from generation to generation, down through the ages, so their children and their children's children's bore gaggling half wits. I would addle their heads, curdling corrupting the insides of their skills until their brains dripped from their noses like bloody mucus.'</i><br /><br /><b>What I liked:</b> This is an incredibly quick read as it is written in short journal entries and the first 100 pages are in sections corresponding to the various journeys she makes on her way to America. <br /><br />The story was really interesting and I was really intrigued by a lot of the main characters. Particularly Mary and her mother The writing and the narrative voice felt very fitting for the character. <br /><br /><b>What I didn't:</b> There wasn't as much magic and witchcraft as I expected there to be, I also would have liked there to be more time spent talking about the Native American people in this novel. But I have a feeling both of these themes will be more prominent in the sequel. <br /><br />Although the first 100 pages is fast paced, the documentation of the journeys does get a little bit repetitive and I would have preferred to know more about Mary and her Grandmother's life in England. <br /><br /><b>Who would I recommend this book to:</b> Everyone who enjoys YA novels with a historical setting or are interested in Salem and the Puritans vs Witchcraft topic and the persecution of women during this time. <br /><br /><b>Rating:</b> 3.5/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="4667734411976276914" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
